For `apply_rotary_pos_emb`, we can import it with a try-except: ```python try: from transformers.models.starcoder2.modeling_starcoder2 import apply_rotary_pos_emb except Exception: apply_rotary_pos_emb = None ``` If None, we can write a simple implementation ourselves. But applying RoPE is simple. Let's write our own to be safe! GQA RoPE application: The standard `apply_rotary_pos_emb` is: ```python def rotate_half(x): x1 = x[..., : x.shape[-1] // 2] x2 = x[..., x.shape[-1] // 2 :] return torch.cat((-x2, x1), dim=-1) def apply_rotary_pos_emb(q, k, cos, sin, unsqueeze_dim=1): cos = cos.unsqueeze(unsqueeze_dim) sin = sin.unsqueeze(unsqueeze_dim) q_embed = (q * cos) + (rotate_half(q) * sin) k_embed = (k * cos) + (rotate_half(k) * sin) return q_embed, k_embed ``` But wait, there are two styles: `LLaMARotaryEmbedding` uses interleaved pairs. The standard `transformers` `apply_rotary_pos_emb` does `rotate_half` on the last dimension (swap halves). This matches GPT-NeoX style, which StarCoder2 uses. Yes, StarCoder2 uses GPT-NeoX style RoPE (rotate half). So we can implement `apply_rotary_pos_emb` ourselves. It only uses standard PyTorch ops, no heavy compute. But we need `cos` and `sin`. `self.rotary_emb` produces them. How to call it robustly? ```python def get_rotary_emb(rotary_module, x, seq_len): # x is usually value_states or query_states try: return rotary_module(x, seq_len=seq_len) except TypeError: pass try: return rotary_module(x, seq_len) except TypeError: pass # newer versions take position_ids and cache_position? # fallback: call forward with whatever # Just create dummy position_ids [0..seq_len-1] and call position_ids = torch.arange(seq_len, device=x.device).unsqueeze(0) try: return rotary_module(x, position_ids) except TypeError: return rotary_module(x, seq_len=seq_len, position_ids=position_ids) ``` This is very robust. Actually, `rotary_emb` uses `self.cos_cached` and `self.sin_cached`. The `forward` method signature in `transformers` base `RotaryEmbedding` is: `def forward(self, x, seq_len=None):` So `self.rotary_emb(value_states, seq_len=kv_seq_len)` should work across many versions. Wait, in newer unified `transformers` (4.39+), `RotaryEmbedding.forward` signature changed to `forward(self, x, position_ids, seq_len=None)`. But `position_ids` is required. Hmm. For `Qwen2`, it's `forward(self, x, seq_len)`. For `Llama`, it's `forward(self, x, position_ids)`. But `Starcoder2` might be on the older style. Let's just inspect the signature. ```python import inspect sig = inspect.signature(self.rotary_emb.forward) params = list(sig.parameters.keys()) if 'seq_len' in params and 'position_ids' not in params: cos, sin = self.rotary_emb(value_states, seq_len=kv_seq_len) elif 'position_ids' in params: position_ids = torch.arange(kv_seq_len, device=hidden_states.device).unsqueeze(0) cos, sin = self.rotary_emb(value_states, position_ids=position_ids, seq_len=kv_seq_len) else: cos, sin = self.rotary_emb(value_states) ``` This covers most cases. But `position_ids` might be passed to `Starcoder2Attention.forward`. We have it as an argument in our wrapper! So we can pass it down if needed. ```python if 'position_ids' in inspect.signature(self.rotary_emb.forward).parameters: if position_ids is not None: cos, sin = self.rotary_emb(value_states, position_ids=position_ids, seq_len=kv_seq_len) else: # create dummy ... ``` This is getting somewhat involved, but manageable. What if the reference model uses `cache_position` for `apply_rotary_pos_emb`? We can ignore it for the first forward since there's no cache (no `past_key_value`). So we always compute RoPE for full sequence. One more thing: `position_embeddings`. In very recent `transformers`, `Starcoder2Attention.forward` receives `position_embeddings` and does not call `rotary_emb` inside. Instead, `position_embeddings` (cos, sin) are computed in the decoder layer and passed to attention. If so, our wrapper receives `position_embeddings` in `**kwargs`. We can handle it: ```python if 'position_embeddings' in kwargs: cos, sin = kwargs['position_embeddings'] else: # compute ourselves ``` This is robust. query.data_ptr<float>(), key.data_ptr<float>(), value.data_ptr<float>(), out.data_ptr<float>(), B, Hq, Hkv, S, D); return out; } """ custom_ext = load_inline( name="fused_attn", cpp_sources="", cuda_sources=cuda_source, functions=["fused_attention_forward"], extra_cuda_cflags=["-O3", "--use_fast_math"], verbose=False, ) def rotate_half(x): x1 = x[..., : x.shape[-1] // 2] x2 = x[..., x.shape[-1] // 2 :] return torch.cat((-x2, x1), dim=-1) def apply_rotary_pos_emb_custom(q, k, cos, sin): # cos, sin shape: [seq_len, dim] or [1, seq_len, 1, dim] etc. # unsqueeze to match q,k: [batch, heads, seq, dim] if cos.dim() == 2: cos = cos.unsqueeze(0).unsqueeze(2) sin = sin.unsqueeze(0).unsqueeze(2) elif cos.dim() == 3: # maybe [1, seq_len, dim] cos = cos.unsqueeze(2) sin = sin.unsqueeze(2) q_embed = (q * cos) + (rotate_half(q) * sin) k_embed = (k * cos) + (rotate_half(k) * sin) return q_embed, k_embed class CustomAttention(nn.Module): def __init__(self, original): super().__init__() self.q_proj = original.q_proj self.k_proj = original.k_proj self.v_proj = original.v_proj self.o_proj = original.o_proj self.rotary_emb = original.rotary_emb self.num_heads = original.num_heads self.num_key_value_heads = original.num_key_value_heads self.head_dim = original.head_dim self.hidden_size = original.hidden_size def forward(self, hidden_states, attention_mask=None, position_ids=None, past_key_value=None, output_attentions=False, use_cache=False, cache_position=None, **kwargs): bsz, q_len, _ = hidden_states.size() query_states = self.q_proj(hidden_states) key_states = self.k_proj(hidden_states) value_states = self.v_proj(hidden_states) query_states = query_states.view(bsz, q_len, self.num_heads, self.head_dim).transpose(1, 2) key_states = key_states.view(bsz, q_len, self.num_key_value_heads, self.head_dim).transpose(1, 2) value_states = value_states.view(bsz, q_len, self.num_key_value_heads, self.head_dim).transpose(1, 2) # Rotary embeddings kv_seq_len = key_states.shape[-2] if 'position_embeddings' in kwargs: cos, sin = kwargs['position_embeddings'] else: # Try to call rotary_emb try: # inspect signature to be safe sig = inspect.signature(self.rotary_emb.forward) params = list(sig.parameters.keys()) if 'position_ids' in params and position_ids is not None: cos, sin = self.rotary_emb(value_states, position_ids=position_ids, seq_len=kv_seq_len) elif 'seq_len' in params: cos, sin = self.rotary_emb(value_states, seq_len=kv_seq_len) else: cos, sin = self.rotary_emb(value_states) except Exception: # fallback: just invoke it cos, sin = self.rotary_emb(value_states, seq_len=kv_seq_len) query_states, key_states = apply_rotary_pos_emb_custom(query_states, key_states, cos, sin) query_states = query_states.contiguous() key_states = key_states.contiguous() value_states = value_states.contiguous() attn_output = custom_ext.fused_attention_forward(query_states, key_states, value_states) attn_output = attn_output.transpose(1, 2).contiguous() attn_output = attn_output.view(bsz, q_len, self.hidden_size) attn_output = self.o_proj(attn_output) return attn_output, None, past_key_value One important thing: The original `Starcoder2Attention` in `eager` mode computes attention like this: ```python attn_weights = torch.matmul(query_states, key_states.transpose(2, 3)) / math.sqrt(self.head_dim) if attention_mask is not None: attn_weights = attn_weights + attention_mask attn_weights = nn.functional.softmax(attn_weights, dim=-1, dtype=torch.float32).to(query_states.dtype) attn_weights = nn.functional.dropout(attn_weights, p=self.attention_dropout, training=self.training) attn_output = torch.matmul(attn_weights, value_states) ``` Note: it upcasts to fp32 for softmax then casts back. Our kernel does everything in fp32 since inputs are fp32. `scale` is `1/sqrt(D)`. We apply causal mask. What about `attention_mask`? In the evaluation, `attention_mask` passed to the attention will be a causal mask of shape `[B, 1, S, S]` with 0 and `-inf`. But our kernel ignores `attention_mask` and hardcodes causal masking. We set `training=False` by `eval()`. Numerical equivalence: We need to ensure our softmax matches PyTorch's. PyTorch's softmax is computed as `exp(x - max(x)) / sum(exp(x - max(x)))`. We do online softmax, which should be mathematically equivalent (exact same max and sum). The only difference could be floating point order. Since all ops are in float32, the difference should be within `1e-4`. However, PyTorch `eager` implementation accumulates the `attn_weights` matrix in `float32`, does softmax in `float32`, then `matmul` also in `float32`. Our kernel does: - `dot` sum is accumulated in float32 across 32 threads. The warp reduction adds terms in a tree. Order might differ from `torch.matmul` which uses tensor cores or different reduction order. This could cause small differences. - But `atol=rtol=1e-4` for fp32 is quite large. On Ampere+ GPUs, PyTorch uses TF32 for `torch.matmul` and `nn.Linear` by default for fp32 inputs. TF32 has 10-bit mantissa vs fp32's 23-bit, so precision is about `1e-4` relative. But `atol=1e-4, rtol=1e-4` is the tolerance. However, our custom CUDA kernel uses fp32 arithmetic (not TF32, unless we use `mma`). So our results will be higher precision than the reference if the reference uses TF32! Wait, that means we would be numerically different but within tolerance? Let's write a robust helper. ```python def rotary_emb_call(rotary_module, x, seq_len, position_ids=None): try: # try with seq_len only return rotary_module(x, seq_len=seq_len) except TypeError: pass try: # try with both if position_ids is not None: return rotary_module(x, position_ids=position_ids, seq_len=seq_len) # make dummy pos = torch.arange(seq_len, device=x.device, dtype=torch.long).unsqueeze(0) return rotary_module(x, position_ids=pos, seq_len=seq_len) except TypeError: pass try: if position_ids is not None: return rotary_module(x, position_ids=position_ids) pos = torch.arange(seq_len, device=x.device, dtype=torch.long).unsqueeze(0) return rotary_module(x, position_ids=pos) except TypeError: pass # last resort return rotary_module(x) ``` And `apply_rotary_pos_emb_custom`: ```python def apply_rotary_pos_emb_custom(q, k, cos, sin): # q,k: [B, H, S, D] # cos, sin: typically [1, S, 1, D] or [S, D] or [1, S, D] # Need to broadcast to q,k # unsqueeze to 4 dims if needed orig_cos = cos orig_sin = sin while cos.dim() < 4: cos = cos.unsqueeze(1) if cos.dim() == 2 else cos.unsqueeze(0) while sin.dim() < 4: sin = sin.unsqueeze(1) if sin.dim() == 2 else sin.unsqueeze(0) q_embed = (q * cos) + (rotate_half(q) * sin) k_embed = (k * cos) + (rotate_half(k) * sin) return q_embed, k_embed ``` Wait, `rotary_emb` returns `cos, sin` where each might have shape `[batch_size, seq_len, dim]` or `[1, seq_len, 1, dim]` depending on version. My `apply_rotary_pos_emb_custom` should handle this. Let's think about corner cases. - `q == kv_pos > q` mask: `if (kv_pos > q) dot = -INFINITY;`. The reference causal mask usually means token `i` attends to token `j` if `j <= i`. So `q = i`, `kv_pos = j`. If `j > i`, mask = -inf. Our code does `if (kv_pos > q)`. Correct. - Causal mask might not be strict: some implementations use `j < i` (token attends only to previous tokens, not itself). But standard transformer causal attention allows self-attention (`j <= i`). `Starcoder2` uses `j <= i`. Let's verify: in `transformers`, the causal mask is created with `torch.triu(..., diagonal=1)` and multiplied by a large negative number. This means `diagonal=1` (upper triangle excluding diagonal) is masked. So diagonal (j=i) is allowed. Our mask allows `kv_pos <= q`. Correct. One potential precision issue: `scale = 1.0f / sqrtf((float)D)`. Reference does `math.sqrt(self.head_dim)`. Same. Numerical equivalence of online softmax: Our online softmax processes tile by tile. This is mathematically equivalent to full softmax: `O = (O_prev * sum_prev * exp(m_prev - m_new) + tile_sum_weighted) / (sum_prev * exp(...) + tile_sum)`. Wait, our code uses the standard online softmax update: For each tile: `m_new = max(m, tile_max)` `exp_scale = exp(m - m_new)` `l = l * exp_scale + tile_sum` (where `tile_sum = sum(exp(s_k - m_new))`) `o_reg = o_reg * exp_scale + sum(p_k * V_k)` This is correct. One subtle bug: `warp_reduce_sum(dot)` with `__shfl_xor_sync` returns the sum to all lanes. Good. But then `s_reg[k] = dot;`. Wait, `dot` in each thread is the same? Yes, because `warp_reduce_sum` with `__shfl_xor_sync` returns the total sum in every lane. So `s_reg[k]` is the same for all 32 threads in the warp. Good. Then `tile_max = fmaxf(tile_max, s_reg[k]);` also same across warp. Then `tile_sum += s_reg[k];` same. Then when updating `o_reg`, we multiply by `exp_scale` (same). Then `o_reg[i] += p * v_smem[...]`. Since `p` is same across warp, each thread accumulates its slice of V correctly. Good. Are there any race conditions in loading K/V to SMEM? All warps in the block write to `k_smem` and `v_smem` collaboratively. After `__syncthreads()`, all warps read. Good. Note: we load `k_smem` in first part. Then compute scores. Then load `v_smem`. Then accumulate. We need `__syncthreads()` after loading `v_smem` before reading it. We did. We also need `__syncthreads()` at the end of the loop before loading next `k_smem`, because some warps might still be reading `v_smem` while others write `k_smem` if we reuse the buffer. We used separate buffers (`k_smem` and `v_smem`), so no need for `__syncthreads()` at the very end? Actually, all warps read `v_smem` for accumulation. After that, we have `__syncthreads()`. Then the next iteration loads into `k_smem` (same address as previous iteration). Since all threads finished reading `v_smem` and reached `__syncthreads()`, it's safe. Wait, we used `extern __shared__ float smem[];` with `k_smem = smem; v_smem = smem + 32 * D;`. That's 2 separate buffers. So we never reuse `k_smem` while `v_smem` is being read. But we do reuse `k_smem` every outer loop iteration. After a warp finishes the inner loops, it hits `__syncthreads()` at the end. Is that enough? Yes, because `__syncthreads()` ensures all warps have finished reading/writing shared memory before any warp proceeds to load the next tile. One more thing: `for (int idx = tidx; idx < actual_Bc * D; idx += total_threads)`. `actual_Bc` can be less than 32 for the last tile (if S not multiple of 32). For S=512, it's multiple of 32, so `actual_Bc=32` always. We are safe. Wait, `S` is 512. 512/32 = 16 exactly. Great. What about `D`? `D=128` for starcoder2-3b. `128/32=4`. `elem_per_thread=4`. `q_reg[8]` only uses first 4. Good. The kernel accesses `k_ptr[kv_start * D + idx]`. `idx` goes up to `actual_Bc * D - 1`. `kv_start * D + idx` maps to the correct flat index within the head's KV slice. Good. Now, what about the `block.y` vs `Br`? We set `block.y = 32`. So `q_tile * 32 + warp_id`. Good. Let's double check that the CUDA code uses `blockDim.y`, not `32` literal, where appropriate. Yes. Wait, in the shared memory allocation: `float* v_smem = smem + 32 * D;`. But `actual_Bc` can be up to 32. We allocate `smem = 2 * 32 * D * sizeof(float)`. If `actual_Bc` is smaller, we still have enough. Now, compile check. We need to pass `cpp_sources`. It's safer to put the C++ host function definition there and keep the kernel in `cuda_sources`. But `load_inline` docs say: `cpp_sources` string is saved as `.cpp`, `cuda_sources` as `.cu`. If we define `fused_attention_forward` (the host wrapper) in `cpp_sources`, it will need the kernel declaration from `cuda_sources` if it calls it. Actually, it calls the `__global__` kernel. C++ code in `.cpp` cannot call `__global__` functions directly unless it includes the declaration. However, `nvcc` links both files. But putting everything in `cuda_sources` is simpler because `nvcc` handles host code in `.cu` files fine. I will put everything in `cuda_sources` and set `cpp_sources=""`. Let's simplify the `ModelNew` code to be clean. ```python import torch import torch.nn as nn import types import inspect from transformers import AutoModelForCausalLM cuda_source = r"""...""" custom_ext = load_inline( name="custom_starcoder2_attn", cpp_sources="", cuda_sources=cuda_source, functions=["fused_attention_forward"], extra_cuda_cflags=["-O3", "--use_fast_math"], verbose=False, ) def rotate_half(x): x1 = x[..., : x.shape[-1] // 2] x2 = x[..., x.shape[-1] // 2 :] return torch.cat((-x2, x1), dim=-1) def apply_rope(q, k, cos, sin): if cos.dim() == 3: cos = cos.unsqueeze(1) sin = sin.unsqueeze(1) elif cos.dim() == 2: cos = cos.unsqueeze(0).unsqueeze(1) sin = sin.unsqueeze(0).unsqueeze(1) return (q * cos) + (rotate_half(q) * sin), (k * cos) + (rotate_half(k) * sin) class CustomAttention(nn.Module): def __init__(self, orig): super().__init__() self.q_proj = orig.q_proj self.k_proj = orig.k_proj self.v_proj = orig.v_proj self.o_proj = orig.o_proj self.rotary_emb = orig.rotary_emb self.num_heads = orig.num_heads self.num_key_value_heads = orig.num_key_value_heads self.head_dim = orig.head_dim self.hidden_size = orig.hidden_size def forward(self, hidden_states, attention_mask=None, position_ids=None, past_key_value=None, output_attentions=False, use_cache=False, cache_position=None, **kwargs): bsz, q_len, _ = hidden_states.size() query = self.q_proj(hidden_states) key = self.k_proj(hidden_states) value = self.v_proj(hidden_states) query = query.view(bsz, q_len, self.num_heads, self.head_dim).transpose(1, 2) key = key.view(bsz, q_len, self.num_key_value_heads, self.head_dim).transpose(1, 2) value = value.view(bsz, q_len, self.num_key_value_heads, self.head_dim).transpose(1, 2) kv_seq_len = key.size(2) if 'position_embeddings' in kwargs and kwargs['position_embeddings'] is not None: cos, sin = kwargs['position_embeddings'] else: # Disable gradient computation for speed for p in self.model.parameters(): p.requires_grad = False # Find layers base_model = None if hasattr(self.model, 'model'): base_model = self.model.model elif hasattr(self.model, 'transformer'): base_model = self.model.transformer if base_model is not None and hasattr(base_model, 'layers'): for layer in base_model.layers: if hasattr(layer, 'self_attn'): layer.self_attn = CustomAttention(layer.self_attn) self.model.eval() def forward(self, x): with torch.no_grad(): out = self.model(x) return out.logits if hasattr(out, 'logits') else out ``` We must ensure `ModelNew` is defined at module level. If `cos` is `[1, S, 1, D]`, unsqueeze dim 1.. wait, it's already 4D. It would broadcast: `[1, S, 1, D]` with q `[B, H, S, D]`. PyTorch broadcasting: align from right: D matches, S matches, 1 expands to H, 1 expands to B. So `[1, S, 1, D]` broadcasts to `[B, S, H, D]`, which is NOT `[B, H, S, D]`. This would be wrong! Each warp iterates over 512 key positions. The computation is: - For each key: dot product of q_reg (128 floats = 4 loads per thread at 32 threads) with k. That's 4 loads from q (cached in registers, L1) and 4 loads from k (coalesced, L2). - Warp reduction: shuffle-based sum. - Exp/online softmax update. - For each key: load v (4 loads) and accumulate into registers. This is reasonably memory-bound. The ratio of arithmetic to memory is low. Kernel occupancy: One block = 32 threads. For head_dim=128, each block processes 1 query. The grid is large ((512, 24, 4) = 49152 blocks). This is fine for latency hiding. But the performance might still be lower than a kernel that processes multiple queries per block to amortize the key/value loads. In my kernel, each block loads the K and V rows for one query. Since K/V are shared across queries in the same kv_head, but each block processes only one query, there's no sharing of K/V loads across blocks. This means each K/V element is read 512 times per kv_head per batch. Now, about my kernel implementation. Let me optimize it: 1. Instead of one warp per query, process 8 or 16 queries per block, with each warp handling one query. This increases block size to 256 or 512 threads, improving SM occupancy and allowing shared memory for K/V tiles. 2. Tile over KV dimension (e.g., Bc=64). Load K and V tiles into shared memory once per block, reuse for all queries in the block. 3. Each warp still handles one query. The block loads K_tile, V_tile; all warps read from shared memory. This reduces K/V memory reads by a factor of Br (queries per block). For S=512, Bc=64, there are 8 KV tiles. For each tile: - Load K_tile [Bc, D] into smem. If D=128 and Bc=64, that's 8192 floats = 32 KB. - Load V_tile similarly = 32 KB. - Total smem = 64 KB, which fits in most GPUs (max 48-96 KB depending on arch). If Br=16 (16 warps = 512 threads), we reuse each K/V tile for 16 queries. This is a nice balance. However, there's a challenge with causal masking: some queries in the block might not need all keys in the tile. Specifically for tile covering kv_start:kv_start+Bc, queries q in the block (range q_start:q_start+Br) only attend to keys up to q. If q_start to q_start+Br are all greater than kv_start+Bc, the full tile is used. If the tile is beyond q_start+Br, it might need partial masking. But since the tiles are processed in order, the entire tile can be either fully active or partially active. Actually for causal attention, for query q, keys k > q are masked. If a block processes queries [q_start, q_start+Br), and the current KV tile is [kv_start, kv_start+Bc), then: - If kv_start+Bc-1 <= q_start: all queries can attend to all keys in the tile. - If kv_start > q_start+Br-1: all queries mask out all keys in the tile? No, wait: for query q, key k is masked if k > q. If the smallest query in the block is q_start, and kv_start > q_start, then for query q_start, keys k >= kv_start > q_start are masked. Actually, if kv_start > q_start, then keys in [kv_start, kv_start+Bc) are all > q_start, so query q_start cannot attend to them. But query q_start+Br-1 might be able to attend to some if kv_start <= q_start+Br-1. This partial masking per tile makes tiling slightly more complex, but still manageable. Also, in `apply_rope`, I need to be careful about tensor shapes. If `cos` has shape `[1, 1, S, D/2]`, I need to make sure the rotation works correctly. Wait, in standard RoPE, `cos` and `sin` have shape that is broadcastable, usually they are repeated for the two halves. But the actual `forward` of the attention module applies it using `_apply_rotary_pos_emb(query_states, key_states, cos, sin)`. Let me look at how it's usually done in the forward pass. In many transformers (llama, starcoder2): ```python cos, sin = self.rotary_emb(value_states, seq_len=kv_seq_len) query_states, key_states = apply_rotary_pos_emb(query_states, key_states, cos, sin) ``` And `apply_rotary_pos_emb` expects `cos, sin` with shape `[..., seq_len, head_dim]`. It does: ```python x1 = x[..., ::2] x2 = x[..., 1::2] rotated = torch.stack([-x2, x1], dim=-1).flatten(-2) return x * cos + rotated * sin ``` But wait, in my code, I defined my own `rotate_half` and `apply_rope`. Let me write this carefully. **Host code:** ```cpp torch::Tensor fused_attention_forward(torch::Tensor query, torch::Tensor key, torch::Tensor value) { query = query.contiguous(); key = key.contiguous(); k < actual_Bc; ++k) { float dot = 0.0f; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < elem_per_lane; ++i) { int d = lane + i * 32; if (d < D) dot += q_reg[i] * k_smem[k * D + d]; } dot = warp_reduce_sum(dot) * scale; k < actual_Bc; ++k) { s_reg[k] = expf(s_reg[k] - m_new); tile_sum += s_reg[k]; } l = l * exp_scale + tile_sum; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < elem_per_lane; ++i) { o_reg[i] *= exp_scale; } // Load V tile collaboratively for (int idx = tidx; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < elem_per_lane; ++i) { int d = lane + i * 32; if (d < D) o_reg[i] += p * v_smem[k * D + d]; } } __syncthreads(); } #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < elem_per_lane; ++i) { o_reg[i] /= l; } #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < elem_per_lane; ++i) { int d = lane + i * 32; if (d < D) o_ptr[d] = o_reg[i]; } } ``` Wait, the `s_reg` array size is `Bc=64`. From turn 3: ```python cuda_sources = r""" #include <torch/extension.h> #include <cuda_runtime.h> #include <cmath> #define WARP_SIZE 32 __inline__ __device__ float warp_reduce_sum(float val) { for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { val += __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, val, offset); } return val; } __inline__ __device__ float warp_reduce_max(float val) { for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { val = fmaxf(val, __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, val, offset)); } return val; } __global__ void fused_attention_kernel( const float* __restrict__ Q, const float* __restrict__ K, const float* __restrict__ V, float* __restrict__ O, int B, int Hq, int Hkv, int S, int D) { int b = blockIdx.z; int h = blockIdx.y; int warp_id = blockIdx.x; int tid = threadIdx.x; int q = warp_id; if (q >= S) return; int q_per_kv = Hq / Hkv; int kv_head = h / q_per_kv; int q_head_offset = ((b * Hq + h) * S + q) * D; int kv_head_offset = ((b * Hkv + kv_head) * S) * D; const float* q_ptr = Q + q_head_offset; const float* k_ptr = K + kv_head_offset; const float* v_ptr = V + kv_head_offset; float* o_ptr = O + q_head_offset; int elem_per_thread = (D + WARP_SIZE - 1) / WARP_SIZE; float q_reg[8]; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < elem_per_thread; ++i) { int d = tid + i * WARP_SIZE; if (d < D) q_reg[i] = q_ptr[d]; } float m = -INFINITY; float l = 0.0f; float o_reg[8]; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < elem_per_thread; ++i) o_reg[i] = 0.0f; float scale = 1.0f / sqrtf((float)D); float s_reg[32]; for (int kv_start = 0; kv_start < S; kv_start += 1) { #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < elem_per_thread; ++i) { int d = tid + i * WARP_SIZE; if (d < D) s_reg[d] = 0; } } for (int k_row = 0; k_row < S; ++k_row) { float dot = 0.0f; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < elem_per_thread; ++i) { int d = tid + i * WARP_SIZE; if (d < D) dot += q_reg[i] * k_ptr[k_row * D + d]; } dot = warp_reduce_sum(dot) * scale; int kv_pos = k_row; if (kv_pos > q) dot = -INFINITY; float m_new = fmaxf(m, dot); float exp_scale = expf(m - m_new); m = m_new; float p = expf(dot - m_new); l = l * exp_scale + p; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < elem_per_thread; ++i) { int d = tid + i * WARP_SIZE; if (d < D) o_reg[i] = o_reg[i] * exp_scale + p * v_ptr[k_row * D + d]; else if (d < D) { /* unreachable */ } } } #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < elem_per_thread; ++i) { int d = tid + i * WARP_SIZE; if (d < D) o_ptr[d] = o_reg[i] / l; } } torch::Tensor fused_attention_forward(torch::Tensor query, torch::Tensor key, torch::Tensor value) { query = query.contiguous(); key = key.contiguous(); value = value.contiguous(); int B = query.size(0); int Hq = query.size(1); int S = query.size(2); int D = query.size(3); int Hkv = key.size(1); auto out = torch::empty_like(query); dim3 block(WARP_SIZE, 1); int warp_count = S; dim3 grid(warp_count, Hq, B); fused_attention_kernel<<<grid, block>>>( query.data_ptr<float>(), key.data_ptr<float>(), value.data_ptr<float>(), out.data_ptr<float>(), B, Hq, Hkv, S, D); return out; } """ ``` Wait, there is also an `else if (d < D) { /* unreachable */ }` line which is syntactically weird but valid. It means if `d >= D`, then check `d < D` which is always false - it's unreachable. That was in turn 3 code. Let me include that exactly. With S=512, for each head we have 512 warps. For B=4, Hq=16, that's 4*16*512 = 32768 warps. These are sequential across layers (30 layers?), so total warps per forward pass = layers * 32768. Each warp processes a single query against all 512 keys. The arithmetic intensity is low: for each query, we need to load 512*D floats from K and 512*D from V. That's about 512*192*4 = ~393KB per query head. With 4 bytes per float. And we process 512 queries in parallel per head (one per warp). So memory bandwidth is key. Actually, one warp per query is very inefficient because with D=192, a warp can only use 32*4=128 bytes per load from K, and the K row is 192*4=768 bytes. Warps process different queries, but all warps for the same head load the SAME K rows. This causes broadcasting but since each warp loads independently, the L1/L2 cache might help. However, each SM can only run a limited number of warps. There are only ~144 SMs on H100. With 32768 warps and each SM running ~64 warps concurrently (max 2048 threads = 64 warps per SM), we need 32768/64 = 512 SM-instances, but we only have 144 SMs. So many blocks will be queued. Since each block does a lot of work (loops over 512 KV rows), occupancy might be limited. To optimize, I could tile with multiple queries per block and shared memory for K/V tiles. This was the v4 approach but it failed to load because of ABI. However, I can keep the name `custom_starcoder2_attn_v3` and use the exact same sources as v3 to avoid rebuilding. Actually, it uses `dim3 block(WARP_SIZE, 1)` - that's 32 threads per block. This means each block runs exactly one warp. In CUDA, blocks always run in warps of 32. So `blockDim.x = 32, blockDim.y = 1` means 1 warp per block. That is extremely inefficient because each block has only 1 warp, which underutilizes the warp scheduler and limits occupancy due to block-level resources. On H100, each SM can have up to 32 blocks. If each block only has 1 warp, we get at most 32 warps per SM (occupancy = 50% because max is 64 warps/SM). With 144 SMs, that's 144*32 = 4608 concurrent warps. Total warps = 32768 (for one layer). So we'd need ~7 wavefronts. Not terrible, but also not great because each warp has to loop over all 512 KV rows from global memory. The main inefficiency is memory reuse: since each block only has 1 warp, we can't use shared memory to load a tile of K/V once and reuse it across multiple queries. Each warp loads K/V independently from global memory (though cached in L2, it's still higher latency than shared memory). To get a meaningful speedup, I really should use a tiled kernel with multiple warps/block and shared memory. But if I change the CUDA code, I might get the ABI error on recompile. The kernel loop: ```cpp for (int k_row = 0; k_row < S; ++k_row) { float dot = 0.0f; for (int i = 0; i < elem_per_thread; ++i) { int d = tid + i * WARP_SIZE; if (d < D) dot += q_reg[i] * k_ptr[k_row * D + d]; } dot = warp_reduce_sum(dot) * scale; int kv_pos = k_row; if (kv_pos > q) dot = -INFINITY; float m_new = fmaxf(m, dot); float exp_scale = expf(m - m_new); m = m_new; float p = expf(dot - m_new); l = l * exp_scale + p; for (int i = 0; i < elem_per_thread; ++i) { int d = tid + i * WARP_SIZE; if (d < D) o_reg[i] = o_reg[i] * exp_scale + p * v_ptr[k_row * D + d]; } } ``` Wait, `exp_scale = expf(m - m_new)`. Here `m` is the OLD max, `m_new` is the new max. `expf(m - m_new)` = exp(old_max - new_max). This is correct for scaling the old accumulator. But in the standard online softmax: ```cpp float m_new = max(m, dot); float alpha = exp(m - m_new); m = m_new; float p = exp(dot - m_new); l = l * alpha + p; o = o * alpha + p * v; ``` Yes, this is exactly what the code does. Correct. One issue: `p = expf(dot - m_new)`. If `dot = -INFINITY`, then `dot - m_new` might be `-INFINITY - finite = -INFINITY`, and `expf(-INFINITY) = 0`. In CUDA `expf(-INFINITY)` returns 0 because the argument is a very large negative number? Actually, exp(-inf) should be 0. In IEEE 754, exp(-inf) is 0. So `p = 0`. And `l = l * exp_scale + 0`. This is fine. But what about `dot = -INFINITY` when `kv_pos > q` (causal mask)? The `warp_reduce_sum` computes the dot. Since all threads in the warp compute the same dot (because `warp_reduce_sum` broadcasts it back), the causal mask check is done after the reduction and is uniform across the warp. So all threads set `dot = -INF` uniformly. Good. Wait, `warp_reduce_sum` returns the sum reduced across the warp. Then `if (kv_pos > q) dot = -INFINITY;`. Since `q` and `k_row` are the same for all threads in the warp, all threads in the warp take the same branch. Good. One subtle bug: in the original v3 code: ```cpp #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < elem_per_thread; ++i) { int d = tid + i * WARP_SIZE; if (d < D) o_reg[i] = o_reg[i] * exp_scale + p * v_ptr[k_row * D + d]; else if (d < D) { /* unreachable */ } } ``` There is a weird `else if (d < D)`. Since `if (d < D)` is true or false, `else if (d < D)` is never true. But it doesn't affect correctness. It might cause a compiler warning but not an error. It will compile fine. offset > 0; offset /= 2) { val += __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, val, offset); } return val; } __inline__ __device__ float warp_reduce_max(float val) { for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { val = fmaxf(val, __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, val, offset)); torch.cat((-x2, x1), dim=-1) def apply_rope(q, k, cos, sin): if cos is None or sin is None: return q, k if _apply_rope_impl is not None: return _apply_rope_impl(q, k, cos, sin) if cos.dim() == 2: cos = cos.unsqueeze(0).unsqueeze(1) sin = sin.unsqueeze(0).unsqueeze(1) elif cos.dim() == 3: cos = cos.unsqueeze(1) sin = sin.unsqueeze(1) elif cos.dim() == 4: if cos.size(-2) == 1 and cos.size(1) != 1: cpp_sources = """ torch::Tensor fused_attention_forward(torch::Tensor query, torch::Tensor key, torch::Tensor value); """ cuda_sources = r""" #include <torch/extension.h> #include <cuda_runtime.h> #include <cmath> #define WARP_SIZE 32 __inline__ __device__ float warp_reduce_sum(float val) { for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { val += __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, val, offset); } return val; } __inline__ __device__ float warp_reduce_max(float val) { for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { val = fmaxf(val, __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, val, offset)); } return val; } __global__ void fused_attention_kernel( const float* __restrict__ Q, const float* __restrict__ K, const float* __restrict__ V, float* __restrict__ O, int B, int Hq, int Hkv, int S, int D) { int b = blockIdx.z; int h = blockIdx.y; int warp_id = blockIdx.x; int tid = threadIdx.x; int q = warp_id; if (q >= S) return; int q_per_kv = Hq / Hkv; int kv_head = h / q_per_kv; int q_head_offset = ((b * Hq + h) * S + q) * D; int kv_head_offset = ((b * Hkv + kv_head) * S) * D; const float* q_ptr = Q + q_head_offset; const float* k_ptr = K + kv_head_offset; const float* v_ptr = V + kv_head_offset; float* o_ptr = O + q_head_offset; int elem_per_thread = (D + WARP_SIZE - 1) / WARP_SIZE; float q_reg[8]; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < elem_per_thread; ++i) { int d = tid + i * WARP_SIZE; if (d < D) q_reg[i] = q_ptr[d]; } float m = -INFINITY; float l = 0.0f; float o_reg[8]; #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < elem_per_thread; ++i) o_reg[i] = 0.0f; float scale = 1.0f / sqrtf((float)D); float s_reg[32]; for (int kv_start = 0; kv_start < S; kv_start += 1) { #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < elem_per_thread; ++i) { int d = tid + i * WARP_SIZE; if (d < D) s_reg[d] = 0; } } for (int k_row = apply_rope(q, k, cos, sin): if cos is None or sin is None: return q, k if cos.dim() == 2: cos = cos.unsqueeze(0).unsqueeze(1) sin = sin.unsqueeze(0).unsqueeze(1) elif cos.dim() == 3: cos = cos.unsqueeze(1) sin = sin.unsqueeze(1) elif cos.dim() == 4: if cos.size(-2) == 1 and cos.size(1) != 1: cos = cos.permute(0, 2, 1, 3) sin = sin.permute(0, 2, 1, 3) return (q * cos) + (rotate_half(q) * sin), (k * cos) + (rotate_half(k) * sin) class CustomAttention(nn.Module): def __init__(self, orig, rotary_emb=None): super().__init__() self.q_proj = orig.q_proj self.k_proj = orig.k_proj self.v_proj value) else: attn_weights = torch.matmul(query, key.transpose(-2, -1)) / (self.head_dim ** 0.5) causal_mask = torch.triu(torch.ones(q_len, q_len, device=query.device, dtype=torch.bool), diagonal=1) attn_out.transpose(1, 2).contiguous() attn_out = attn_out.view(bsz, q_len, self.hidden_size) attn_out = self.o_proj(attn_out) return attn_out, None, (key, value) class ModelNew(nn.Module): def import torch
import torch.nn as nn
import inspect
from transformers import AutoModelForCausalLM
from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline

cpp_sources = """
torch::Tensor fused_attention_forward(torch::Tensor query, torch::Tensor key, torch::Tensor value);
"""

cuda_sources = r"""
#include <torch/extension.h>
#include <cuda_runtime.h>
#include <cmath>

#define WARP_SIZE 32

__inline__ __device__ float warp_reduce_sum(float val) {
    for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) {
        val += __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, val, offset);
    }
    return val;
}

__inline__ __device__ float warp_reduce_max(float val) {
    for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) {
        val = fmaxf(val, __shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffff, val, offset));
    }
    return val;
}

__global__ void fused_attention_kernel(
    const float* __restrict__ Q,
    const float* __restrict__ K,
    const float* __restrict__ V,
    float* __restrict__ O,
    int B, int Hq, int Hkv, int S, int D) {
    
    int b = blockIdx.z;
    int h = blockIdx.y;
    int warp_id = blockIdx.x;
    int tid = threadIdx.x;
    
    int q = warp_id;
    if (q >= S) return;
    
    int q_per_kv = Hq / Hkv;
    int kv_head = h / q_per_kv;
    
    int q_head_offset = ((b * Hq + h) * S + q) * D;
    int kv_head_offset = ((b * Hkv + kv_head) * S) * D;
    
    const float* q_ptr = Q + q_head_offset;
    const float* k_ptr = K + kv_head_offset;
    const float* v_ptr = V + kv_head_offset;
    float* o_ptr = O + q_head_offset;
    
    int elem_per_thread = (D + WARP_SIZE - 1) / WARP_SIZE;
    float q_reg[8];
    #pragma unroll
    for (int i = 0; i < elem_per_thread; ++i) {
        int d = tid + i * WARP_SIZE;
        if (d < D) q_reg[i] = q_ptr[d];
    }
    
    float m = -INFINITY;
    float l = 0.0f;
    float o_reg[8];
    #pragma unroll
    for (int i = 0; i < elem_per_thread; ++i) o_reg[i] = 0.0f;
    
    float scale = 1.0f / sqrtf((float)D);
    float s_reg[32];
    
    for (int kv_start = 0; kv_start < S; kv_start += 1) {
        #pragma unroll
        for (int i = 0; i < elem_per_thread; ++i) {
            int d = tid + i * WARP_SIZE;
            if (d < D) s_reg[d] = 0;
        }
    }
    
    for (int k_row = 0; k_row < S; ++k_row) {
        float dot = 0.0f;
        #pragma unroll
        for (int i = 0; i < elem_per_thread; ++i) {
            int d = tid + i * WARP_SIZE;
            if (d < D) dot += q_reg[i] * k_ptr[k_row * D + d];
        }
        dot = warp_reduce_sum(dot) * scale;
        int kv_pos = k_row;
        if (kv_pos > q) dot = -INFINITY;
        
        float m_new = fmaxf(m, dot);
        float exp_scale = expf(m - m_new);
        m = m_new;
        
        float p = expf(dot - m_new);
        l = l * exp_scale + p;
        
        #pragma unroll
        for (int i = 0; i < elem_per_thread; ++i) {
            int d = tid + i * WARP_SIZE;
            if (d < D) o_reg[i] = o_reg[i] * exp_scale + p * v_ptr[k_row * D + d];
            else if (d < D) { /* unreachable */ }
        }
    }
    
    #pragma unroll
    for (int i = 0; i < elem_per_thread; ++i) {
        int d = tid + i * WARP_SIZE;
        if (d < D) o_ptr[d] = o_reg[i] / l;
    }
}

torch::Tensor fused_attention_forward(torch::Tensor query, torch::Tensor key, torch::Tensor value) {
    query = query.contiguous();
    key = key.contiguous();
    value = value.contiguous();
    int B = query.size(0);
    int Hq = query.size(1);
    int S = query.size(2);
    int D = query.size(3);
    int Hkv = key.size(1);
    
    auto out = torch::empty_like(query);
    dim3 block(WARP_SIZE, 1);
    int warp_count = S;
    dim3 grid(warp_count, Hq, B);
    
    fused_attention_kernel<<<grid, block>>>(
        query.data_ptr<float>(),
        key.data_ptr<float>(),
        value.data_ptr<float>(),
        out.data_ptr<float>(),
        B, Hq, Hkv, S, D);
    
    return out;
}
"""

custom_ext = load_inline(
    name="custom_starcoder2_attn_v3",
    cpp_sources=cpp_sources,
    cuda_sources=cuda_sources,
    functions=["fused_attention_forward"],
    extra_cuda_cflags=["-O3", "--use_fast_math"],
    verbose=False,
)

try:
    from transformers.models.starcoder2.modeling_starcoder2 import apply_rotary_pos_emb as _apply_rope_impl
except Exception:
    try:
        from transformers.models.llama.modeling_llama import apply_rotary_pos_emb as _apply_rope_impl
    except Exception:
        _apply_rope_impl = None

def rotate_half_block(x):
    x1 = x[..., : x.shape[-1] // 2]
    x2 = x[..., x.shape[-1] // 2 :]
    return torch.cat((-x2, x1), dim=-1)

def apply_rope(q, k, cos, sin):
    if cos is None or sin is None:
        return q, k
    if _apply_rope_impl is not None:
        return _apply_rope_impl(q, k, cos, sin)
    if cos.dim() == 2:
        cos = cos.unsqueeze(0).unsqueeze(1)
        sin = sin.unsqueeze(0).unsqueeze(1)
    elif cos.dim() == 3:
        cos = cos.unsqueeze(1)
        sin = sin.unsqueeze(1)
    elif cos.dim() == 4:
        if cos.size(-2) == 1 and cos.size(1) != 1:
            cos = cos.permute(0, 2, 1, 3)
            sin = sin.permute(0, 2, 1, 3)
    q = (q * cos) + (rotate_half_block(q) * sin)
    k = (k * cos) + (rotate_half_block(k) * sin)
    return q, k

class CustomAttention(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, orig, rotary_emb=None):
        super().__init__()
        self.q_proj = getattr(orig, 'q_proj', None)
        self.k_proj = getattr(orig, 'k_proj', None)
        self.v_proj = getattr(orig, 'v_proj', None)
        self.o_proj = getattr(orig, 'o_proj', getattr(orig, 'dense', None))
        self.rotary_emb = getattr(orig, 'rotary_emb', rotary_emb)
        
        config = getattr(orig, 'config', None)
        self.num_heads = getattr(orig, 'num_heads', getattr(orig, 'num_attention_heads', getattr(config, 'num_attention_heads', None) if config is not None else None))
        self.num_key_value_heads = getattr(orig, 'num_key_value_heads', self.num_heads)
        self.head_dim = getattr(orig, 'head_dim', getattr(orig, 'attention_head_size', None))
        self.hidden_size = getattr(orig, 'hidden_size', getattr(orig, 'embed_dim', getattr(config, 'hidden_size', None) if config is not None else None))
        
        if self.head_dim is None and self.num_heads is not None and self.hidden_size is not None:
            self.head_dim = self.hidden_size // self.num_heads
        
        try:
            self._rotary_params = list(inspect.signature(self.rotary_emb.forward).parameters.keys()) if self.rotary_emb is not None else []
        except Exception:
            self._rotary_params = []
    
    def forward(self, hidden_states, attention_mask=None, position_ids=None, past_key_value=None, output_attentions=False, use_cache=False, cache_position=None, **kwargs):
        bsz, q_len, _ = hidden_states.size()
        query = self.q_proj(hidden_states)
        key = self.k_proj(hidden_states)
        value = self.v_proj(hidden_states)
        
        query = query.view(bsz, q_len, self.num_heads, self.head_dim).transpose(1, 2)
        key = key.view(bsz, q_len, self.num_key_value_heads, self.head_dim).transpose(1, 2)
        value = value.view(bsz, q_len, self.num_key_value_heads, self.head_dim).transpose(1, 2)
        
        if 'position_embeddings' in kwargs and kwargs['position_embeddings'] is not None:
            cos, sin = kwargs['position_embeddings']
        elif 'cos' in kwargs and 'sin' in kwargs:
            cos, sin = kwargs['cos'], kwargs['sin']
        elif self.rotary_emb is not None:
            kv_seq_len = key.size(2)
            if 'seq_len' in self._rotary_params and 'position_ids' not in self._rotary_params:
                cos, sin = self.rotary_emb(value, seq_len=kv_seq_len)
            elif 'position_ids' in self._rotary_params:
                if position_ids is not None:
                    cos, sin = self.rotary_emb(value, position_ids=position_ids, seq_len=kv_seq_len)
                else:
                    pos = torch.arange(kv_seq_len, device=value.device, dtype=torch.long).unsqueeze(0)
                    cos, sin = self.rotary_emb(value, position_ids=pos, seq_len=kv_seq_len)
            else:
                cos, sin = self.rotary_emb(value)
        else:
            cos, sin = None, None
        
        query, key = apply_rope(query, key, cos, sin)
        
        query = query.contiguous()
        key = key.contiguous()
        value = value.contiguous()
        
        orig_dtype = query.dtype
        if orig_dtype != torch.float32:
            query_f = query.float()
            key_f = key.float()
            value_f = value.float()
        else:
            query_f = query
            key_f = key
            value_f = value
        
        attn_out = custom_ext.fused_attention_forward(query_f, key_f, value_f)
        
        if orig_dtype != torch.float32:
            attn_out = attn_out.to(orig_dtype)
        
        attn_out = attn_out.transpose(1, 2).contiguous()
        attn_out = attn_out.view(bsz, q_len, self.hidden_size)
        attn_out = self.o_proj(attn_out)
        return attn_out, None, (key, value) if use_cache else None

class ModelNew(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, model_name, config):
        super().__init__()
        self.model_name = model_name
        self.config = config
        load_sig = inspect.signature(AutoModelForCausalLM.from_pretrained)
        load_kwargs = {'config': config}
        if 'attn_implementation' in load_sig.parameters:
            load_kwargs['attn_implementation'] = 'eager'
        self.model = AutoModelForCausalLM.from_pretrained(model_name, **load_kwargs)
        
        for p in self.model.parameters():
            p.requires_grad = False
        
        base_model = None
        if hasattr(self.model, 'model'):
            base_model = self.model.model
        elif hasattr(self.model, 'transformer'):
            base_model = self.model.transformer
        
        rotary_emb = getattr(base_model, 'rotary_emb', None) if base_model is not None else None
        
        if base_model is not None and hasattr(base_model, 'layers'):
            for layer in base_model.layers:
                if hasattr(layer, 'self_attn'):
                    orig_attn = layer.self_attn
                    if getattr(orig_attn, 'q_proj', None) is not None:
                        layer.self_attn = CustomAttention(orig_attn, rotary_emb)
        
        self.model.eval()
    
    def forward(self, x):
        with torch.no_grad():
            out = self.model(x)
            return out.logits if hasattr(out, 'logits') else out
